Other groups of rights</th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">

</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Rights" title="Template:Rights"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Rights" title="Template talk:Rights"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Rights&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Reproductive rights</b> are <a href="/wiki/Legal_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal right">legal rights</a> and freedoms relating to <a href="/wiki/Human_reproduction" title="Human reproduction">reproduction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">reproductive health</a> that vary amongst countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-COOK_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COOK-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> defines reproductive rights as follows:
</p>
<blockquote><p>
Reproductive rights rest on the recognition of the basic right of all couples and individuals to decide freely and responsibly the number, spacing and timing of their children and to have the information and means to do so, and the right to attain the highest standard of sexual and reproductive health. They also include the right of all to make decisions concerning reproduction free of <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violence" title="Violence">violence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Women's reproductive rights may include some or all of the following: the <a href="/wiki/Abortion-rights_movements" title="Abortion-rights movements">right to legal and safe abortion</a>; the right to <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a>; freedom from <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">coerced sterilization</a> and contraception; the right to access good-quality <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">reproductive healthcare</a>; and the right to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">education and access</a> in order to make free and informed reproductive choices.<sup id="cite_ref-AMNESTY_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMNESTY-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Reproductive rights may also include the right to receive <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">education</a> about <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexually transmitted disease">sexually transmitted infections</a> and other aspects of sexuality, and protection from practices such as <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM).<sup id="cite_ref-COOK_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COOK-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AMNESTY_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMNESTY-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FREEDMAN-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reproductive rights began to develop as a subset of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> at the United Nation's 1968 International Conference on Human Rights.<sup id="cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FREEDMAN-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non binding</a> Proclamation of Teheran was the first international document to recognize one of these rights when it stated that: "Parents have a basic human right to determine <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">freely</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moral_responsibility" title="Moral responsibility">responsibly</a> the number and the spacing of their children."<sup id="cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FREEDMAN-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teheran_proc_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teheran_proc-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> States, though, have been slow in incorporating these rights in <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">internationally legally binding instruments</a>. Thus, while some of these rights have already been recognized in <a href="/wiki/Soft_law" title="Soft law">hard law</a>, that is, in legally binding <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_instruments" title="International human rights instruments">international human rights instruments</a>, others have been mentioned only in non binding recommendations and, therefore, have at best the status of <a href="/wiki/Soft_law" title="Soft law">soft law</a> in <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, while a further group is yet to be accepted by the international community and therefore remains at the level of <a href="/wiki/Advocacy" title="Advocacy">advocacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Issues related to reproductive rights are some of the most vigorously contested rights' issues worldwide, regardless of the population's <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socioeconomic">socioeconomic</a> level, <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> or <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The issue of reproductive rights is frequently presented as being of vital importance in discussions and articles by <a href="/wiki/List_of_population_concern_organizations" title="List of population concern organizations">population concern organizations</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Population_Matters" title="Population Matters">Population Matters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-popsearch_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popsearch-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reproductive rights are a subset of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_and_reproductive_health_and_rights" title="Sexual and reproductive health and rights">sexual and reproductive health and rights</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proclamation_of_Teheran">Proclamation of Teheran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Proclamation of Teheran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1945, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a> included the obligation "to promote... universal respect for, and observance of, human rights and fundamental freedoms for all without discrimination as to race, sex, language, or religion". However, the Charter did not define these rights. Three years later, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> adopted the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> (UDHR), the first international legal document to delineate <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>; the UDHR does not mention reproductive rights.  Reproductive rights began to appear as a subset of human rights in the 1968 Proclamation of Teheran, which states: "Parents have a basic human right to determine freely and responsibly the number and the spacing of their children".<sup id="cite_ref-teheran_proc_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teheran_proc-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This right was affirmed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> in the 1969 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Declaration_on_Social_Progress_and_Development&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Declaration on Social Progress and Development (page does not exist)">Declaration on Social Progress and Development</a> which states "The family as a basic unit of society and the natural environment for the growth and well-being of all its members, particularly children and youth, should be assisted and protected so that it may fully assume its responsibilities within the community. Parents have the exclusive right to determine freely and responsibly the number and spacing of their children."<sup id="cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FREEDMAN-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Year#International" title="International Women&#39;s Year">1975 UN International Women's Year Conference</a> echoed the Proclamation of Teheran.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_Programme_of_Action">Cairo Programme of Action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cairo Programme of Action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The twenty-year "Cairo Programme of Action" was adopted in 1994 at the <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_on_Population_and_Development" title="International Conference on Population and Development">International Conference on Population and Development</a> (ICPD) in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding</a> Programme of Action asserted that governments have a responsibility to meet individuals' reproductive needs, rather than demographic targets. It recommended that <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> services be provided in the context of other reproductive health services, including services for healthy and safe childbirth, care for sexually transmitted infections, and post-abortion care. The ICPD also addressed issues such as <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking" title="Sex trafficking">sex trafficking</a>, and adolescent health.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudsen_2006_5–6_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudsen_2006_5–6-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Cairo Program is the first international policy document to define <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">reproductive health</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Knudsen_2006_5–6_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudsen_2006_5–6-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> stating:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Reproductive health is a state of complete physical, mental and social well-being and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity, in all matters relating to the reproductive system and its functions and processes. Reproductive health therefore implies that people are able to have a satisfying and safe sex life and that they have the capability to reproduce and the freedom to decide if, when and how often to do so. Implicit in this last condition are the right of men and women to be informed [about] and to have access to safe, effective, affordable and acceptable methods of family planning of their choice, as well as other methods for regulation of fertility which are not against the law, and the right of access to appropriate health-care services that will enable women to go safely through pregnancy and childbirth and provide couples with the best chance of having a healthy infant [para. 72].<sup id="cite_ref-COOK_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COOK-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Unlike previous population conferences, a wide range of interests from grassroots to government level were represented in Cairo. 179 nations attended the ICPD and overall eleven thousand representatives from governments, <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a>, international agencies and citizen activists participated.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudsen_2006_5–6_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudsen_2006_5–6-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The ICPD did not address the far-reaching implications of the <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Epidemiology of HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS epidemic</a>. In 1999, recommendations at the ICPD+5 were expanded to include commitment to AIDS education, research, and prevention of mother-to-child transmission, as well as to the development of vaccines and microbicides.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudsen_2006_7_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudsen_2006_7-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Cairo Programme of Action was adopted by 184 UN member states. Nevertheless, many Latin American and Islamic states made <a href="/wiki/Reservation_(law)" title="Reservation (law)">formal reservations</a> to the programme, in particular, to its concept of reproductive rights and sexual freedom, to its treatment of abortion, and to its potential incompatibility with <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beijing_Platform">Beijing Platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Beijing Platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1995 <a href="/wiki/Fourth_World_Conference_on_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Fourth World Conference on Women">Fourth World Conference on Women</a> in Beijing, in its <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding</a> <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Declaration" title="Beijing Declaration">Declaration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Platform_for_Action" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Platform for Action">Platform for Action</a>, supported the Cairo Programme's definition of reproductive health, but established a broader context of reproductive rights:
</p>
<blockquote><p>The human rights of women include their right to have control over and decide freely and responsibly on matters related to their sexuality, including sexual and reproductive health, free of coercion, discrimination and violence. Equal relationships between women and men in matters of sexual relations and reproduction, including full respect for the integrity of the person, require mutual respect, consent and shared responsibility for sexual behavior and its consequences [para. 96].<sup id="cite_ref-COOK_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COOK-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p> The Beijing Platform demarcated twelve interrelated critical areas of the human rights of women that require advocacy. The Platform framed women's reproductive rights as "indivisible, universal and inalienable human rights."<sup id="cite_ref-BUNCH_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUNCH-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yogyakarta_Principles">Yogyakarta Principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Yogyakarta Principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta_Principles" title="Yogyakarta Principles">Yogyakarta Principles</a> on the Application of International Human Rights Law in relation to Sexual Orientation and Gender Identity, proposed by a group of experts in November 2006<sup id="cite_ref-YOGYABOUT_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YOGYABOUT-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> but not yet incorporated by States in international law,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> declares in its Preamble that "the <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">international community</a> has recognized the rights of persons to decide freely and responsibly on matters related to their sexuality, including sexual and reproductive health, free from coercion, discrimination, and violence." In relation to reproductive health, Principle 9 on "The Right to Treatment with Humanity while in Detention" requires that "States shall... [p]rovide adequate access to medical care and counseling appropriate to the needs of those in custody, recognizing any particular needs of persons on the basis of their sexual orientation and gender identity, including with regard to reproductive health, access to <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> information and therapy and access to <a href="/wiki/Hormone_therapy" title="Hormone therapy">hormonal</a> or other therapy as well as to <a href="/wiki/Sex_reassignment_therapy" title="Sex reassignment therapy">gender-reassignment treatments</a> where desired."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, African, Caribbean and Islamic Countries, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>, have objected to the use of these principles as Human Rights standards.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_abuses">State abuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: State abuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>State abuses against reproductive rights have happened both under right-wing and left-wing governments. Such abuses include attempts to forcefully increase the birth rate - one of the most notorious <a href="/wiki/Natalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Natalist">natalist</a> policies of the 20th century was that which occurred in <a href="/wiki/Communist_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Romania">communist Romania</a> in the period of 1967-1990 during communist leader <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>, who adopted a very aggressive natalist policy which included outlawing abortion and contraception, routine pregnancy tests for women, <a href="/wiki/Tax_on_childlessness" title="Tax on childlessness">taxes on childlessness</a>, and legal discrimination against childless people - as well as attempts to decrease the fertility rate - <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>'s <a href="/wiki/One_child_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="One child policy">one child policy</a> (1978-2015). State mandated <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a> was also practiced by authoritarian governments as a way to meet population targets: the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> regime in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> systematically forced people into marriages, in order to increase the population and continue the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Some governments have implemented <a href="/wiki/Eugenic" class="mw-redirect" title="Eugenic">eugenic</a> policies of <a href="/wiki/Forced_sterilizations" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced sterilizations">forced sterilizations</a> of 'undesirable' population groups. Such policies were carried out against ethnic minorities in Europe and North America in the 20th century, and more recently in Latin America against the Indigenous population in the 1990s; in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, President <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fujimori" title="Alberto Fujimori">Alberto Fujimori</a> (in office from 1990 to 2000) has been accused of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> as a result of a sterilization program put in place by his administration targeting indigenous people (mainly the <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechuas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaras</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first legal textbook on reproductive rights law, <i>Cases on Reproductive Rights and Justice</i> by Melissa Murray and Kristin Luker, was published in 2015 by Foundation Press.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prohibition_of_forced_sterilization_and_forced_abortion">Prohibition of forced sterilization and forced abortion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Prohibition of forced sterilization and forced abortion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_preventing_and_combating_violence_against_women_and_domestic_violence" title="Convention on preventing and combating violence against women and domestic violence">Istanbul convention</a>, the first legally binding instrument in Europe in the field of violence against women and domestic violence<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> prohibits <a href="/wiki/Forced_sterilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced sterilization">forced sterilization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forced_abortion" title="Forced abortion">forced abortion</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Article 39 – Forced abortion and forced sterilisation
</p><dl><dd>Parties shall take the necessary legislative or other measures to ensure that the following intentional conducts are criminalised:</dd></dl>
<ul><li>a performing an abortion on a woman without her prior and informed consent;</li>
<li>b performing surgery which has the purpose or effect of terminating a woman’s capacity to naturally reproduce without her prior and informed consent or understanding of the procedure</li></ul>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Family_planning_Ethiopia_(good_effects).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG/220px-Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG/330px-Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG/440px-Family_planning_Ethiopia_%28good_effects%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Family_planning_Ethiopia_(good_effects).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Placard showing positive effects of <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> (Ethiopia)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">Human rights</a></div><p>
Since most existing legally binding <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_instruments" title="International human rights instruments">international human rights instruments</a> do not explicitly mention sexual and reproductive rights, a <a href="/wiki/Epistemic_community_(international_relations)" title="Epistemic community (international relations)">broad coalition</a> of NGOs, civil servants, and experts working in <a href="/wiki/International_organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="International organizations">international organizations</a> have been promoting a reinterpretation of those instruments to link the realization of the already internationally recognized human rights with the realization of reproductive rights.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> An example of this linkage is provided by the 1994 Cairo Programme of Action: </p><blockquote><p>
Reproductive rights embrace certain human rights that are already recognized in national laws, international human rights documents and other relevant United Nations consensus documents. These rights rest on the recognition of the basic right of all couples and individuals to decide freely and responsibly the number, spacing and timing of their children and to have the information and means to do so, and the right to attain the highest standard of sexual and reproductive health. It also includes the right of all to make decisions concerning reproduction free of discrimination, coercion and violence as expressed in human rights documents. In the exercise of this right, they should take into account the needs of their living and future children and their responsibilities towards the community.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>
Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> has argued that the realisation of reproductive rights is linked with the realisation of a series of recognised <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_health" title="Right to health">right to health</a>, the right to freedom from <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_privacy" title="Right to privacy">right to privacy</a>, and the right not to be subjected to torture or ill-treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-AMNESTY_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMNESTY-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> However, not all states have accepted the inclusion of reproductive rights in the body of internationally recognized human rights. At the Cairo Conference, several states made <a href="/wiki/Reservation_(law)" title="Reservation (law)">formal reservations</a> either to the concept of reproductive rights or to its specific content.  <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, for instance, stated that: </p><blockquote><p>
With regard to the Programme of Action of the Cairo International Conference on Population and Development and in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution and laws of Ecuador and the norms of international law, the delegation of Ecuador reaffirms, inter alia, the following principles embodied in its Constitution:  the inviolability of life, the protection of children from the moment of conception, freedom of conscience and religion, the protection of the family as the fundamental unit of society, responsible paternity, the right of parents to bring up their children and the formulation of population and development plans by the Government in accordance with the principles of respect for sovereignty. Accordingly, the delegation of Ecuador enters a reservation with respect to all terms such as "regulation of fertility", "interruption of pregnancy", "reproductive health", "reproductive rights" and "unwanted children", which in one way or another, within the context of the Programme of Action, could involve abortion.<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Similar reservations were made by <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>. Islamic Countries, such as <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> made broad reservations against any element of the programme that could be interpreted as contrary to the <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a>. Guatemala even questioned whether the conference could legally proclaim new human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Women.27s_rights"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_rights">Women's rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Women&#039;s rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Women%E2%80%99s_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Women’s rights">Women’s rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_justice" title="Reproductive justice">Reproductive justice</a></div>
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%"><tbody><tr><td style="padding-top:0.4em;line-height:1.2em">Part of <a href="/wiki/Category:Feminism" title="Category:Feminism">a series</a> on</td></tr><tr><th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;padding-top:0;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">Feminism</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em"><a href="/wiki/File:Womanpower_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="Womanpower logo.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Womanpower_logo.svg/100px-Womanpower_logo.svg.png" width="100" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Womanpower_logo.svg/150px-Womanpower_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Womanpower_logo.svg/200px-Womanpower_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2931" data-file-height="4103" /></a></td></tr><tr><td class="hlist" style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">

</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<a href="/wiki/File:Woman-power_emblem.svg" class="image"><img alt="Woman-power emblem.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/17px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png" width="17" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/26px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/34px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="1048" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Feminism" title="Portal:Feminism">Feminism&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Feminism_sidebar" title="Template:Feminism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Feminism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Feminism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Feminism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> (UNFPA) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) advocate for reproductive rights with a primary emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women&#39;s rights">women's rights</a>. In this respect the UN and WHO focus on a range of issues from access to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> services, sex education, <a href="/wiki/Menopause" title="Menopause">menopause</a>, and the reduction of <a href="/wiki/Obstetric_fistula" title="Obstetric fistula">obstetric fistula</a>, to the relationship between reproductive health and economic status.
</p><p>The reproductive rights of women are advanced in the context of the right to freedom from <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a> and the social and economic status of women. The group Development Alternatives with Women for a New Era (DAWN) explained the link in the following statement:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Control over reproduction is a basic need and a basic right for all women. Linked as it is to women's health and social status, as well as the powerful social structures of religion, state control and administrative inertia, and private profit, it is from the perspective of poor women that this right can best be understood and affirmed. Women know that childbearing is a social, not a purely personal, phenomenon; nor do we deny that world population trends are likely to exert considerable pressure on resources and institutions by the end of this century. But our bodies have become a pawn in the struggles among states, religions, male heads of households, and private corporations. Programs that do not take the interests of women into account are unlikely to succeed...<sup id="cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FREEDMAN-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Women's reproductive rights have long retained key issue status in the debate on <a href="/wiki/Overpopulation" title="Overpopulation">overpopulation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-popsearch_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popsearch-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>"The only ray of hope I can see – and it's not much – is that wherever women are put in control of their lives, both politically and socially; where medical facilities allow them to deal with birth control and where their husbands allow them to make those decisions, birth rate falls. Women don't want to have 12 kids of whom nine will die." <i><a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">David&#160;Attenborough</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></i></p></blockquote>
<p>Attempts have been made to analyse the socioeconomic conditions that affect the realisation of a woman's reproductive rights. The term <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_justice" title="Reproductive justice">reproductive justice</a> has been used to describe these broader social and economic issues. Proponents of reproductive justice argue that while the right to <a href="/wiki/Abortion_law" title="Abortion law">legalized abortion</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and contraception applies to everyone, these choices are only meaningful to those with resources, and that there is a growing gap between access and affordability.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">Domestic violence</a> (<a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence_against_men" title="Domestic violence against men">against men</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Violence_against_LGBT_people" title="Violence against LGBT people">Violence against LGBT people</a></li></ul>
<div class="hlist">
<ul><li>(<span style="font-size:90%;"><a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">Homophobia</a></span></li>
<li><span style="font-size:90%;"><a href="/wiki/Gay_bashing" title="Gay bashing">Gay bashing</a></span></li>
<li><span style="font-size:90%;"><a href="/wiki/Transphobia" title="Transphobia">Transphobia</a></span>)</li></ul>
</div>

</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_mars.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol mars.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Symbol_mars.svg/28px-Symbol_mars.svg.png" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Symbol_mars.svg/43px-Symbol_mars.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Symbol_mars.svg/57px-Symbol_mars.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="394" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Men%27s_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Portal:Men&#39;s rights">Men's rights&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Masculism_sidebar" title="Template:Masculism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Masculism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Masculism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Masculism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Men's reproductive rights have been claimed by various organizations, both for issues of reproductive health, and other rights related to sexual reproduction.
</p><p>Three international issues in men's reproductive health are <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexually transmitted disease">sexually transmitted diseases</a>, cancer and exposure to <a href="/wiki/Toxins" class="mw-redirect" title="Toxins">toxins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NETWORK_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NETWORK-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recently men's reproductive right with regards to paternity have become subject of debate in the U.S.  The term "<a href="/wiki/Male_abortion" class="mw-redirect" title="Male abortion">male abortion</a>" was coined by Melanie McCulley, a South Carolina attorney, in a 1998 article.  The theory begins with the premise that when a woman becomes pregnant she has the option of abortion, adoption, or parenthood; it argues, in the context of legally recognized <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, that in the earliest stages of pregnancy the putative (alleged) father should have the right to relinquish all future parental rights and financial responsibility, leaving the informed mother with the same three options.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> This concept has been supported by a former president of the feminist organization <a href="/wiki/National_Organization_for_Women" title="National Organization for Women">National Organization for Women</a>, attorney <a href="/wiki/Karen_DeCrow" title="Karen DeCrow">Karen DeCrow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Feminist" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist">feminist</a> argument for male reproductive choice contends that the uneven ability to choose experienced by men and women in regards to parenthood is evidence of a state-enforced <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a> favoring traditional <a href="/wiki/Sex_roles" class="mw-redirect" title="Sex roles">sex roles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, the National Center for Men brought a case in the US, <i><a href="/wiki/Dubay_v._Wells" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubay v. Wells">Dubay v. Wells</a></i> (dubbed by some "<i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i> for men"), that argued that in the event of an unplanned pregnancy, when an unmarried woman informs a man that she is pregnant by him, he should have an opportunity to give up all paternity rights and responsibilities.  Supporters argue that this would allow the woman time to make an informed decision and give men the same reproductive rights as women.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  In its dismissal of the case, the U.S. Court of Appeals (Sixth Circuit) stated that "the Fourteenth Amendment does not deny to [the] State the power to treat different classes of persons in different ways."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The opportunity to give men the right for a <a href="/wiki/Paper_Abortion" class="mw-redirect" title="Paper Abortion">Paper Abortion</a> is heavily discussed.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Intersex_and_reproductive_rights">Intersex and reproductive rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Intersex and reproductive rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Intersex" title="Intersex">Intersex</a></div>
<p>Intersex, in <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humans</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a>, is a variation in <a href="/wiki/Sex" title="Sex">sex</a> characteristics including <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonad" title="Gonad">gonads</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Genital" class="mw-redirect" title="Genital">genitals</a> that do not allow an individual to be distinctly identified as male or female. Such variation may involve genital ambiguity, and combinations of chromosomal <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">genotype</a> and sexual <a href="/wiki/Phenotype" title="Phenotype">phenotype</a> other than XY-male and XX-female.<sup id="cite_ref-Money_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Money-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dreger_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dreger-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Intersex persons are often subjected to involuntary "sex normalizing" surgical and hormonal treatments in infancy and childhood, often also including sterilization.<sup id="cite_ref-coe1952_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe1952-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SenateOnSterilisation_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SenateOnSterilisation-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-swissnek_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swissnek-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UN agencies have begun to take note. On 1 February 2013, Juan E Mendés, the UN Special Rapporteur on torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment or punishment, issued a statement condemning non-consensual surgical intervention on intersex people. His report stated, "Children who are born with atypical sex characteristics are often subject to irreversible sex assignment, involuntary sterilization, involuntary genital normalizing surgery, performed without their informed consent, or that of their parents, "in an attempt to fix their sex", leaving them with permanent, irreversible infertility and causing severe mental suffering".<sup id="cite_ref-untorture_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-untorture-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In May 2014, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> issued a joint statement on <i>Eliminating forced, coercive and otherwise involuntary sterilization, An interagency statement</i> with the <a href="/wiki/OHCHR" class="mw-redirect" title="OHCHR">OHCHR</a>, <a href="/wiki/UN_Women" title="UN Women">UN Women</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNAIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNFPA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFPA">UNFPA</a> and <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>. The report references the involuntary surgical "sex-normalising or other procedures" on "intersex persons". It questions the medical necessity of such treatments, patients' ability to consent, and a weak evidence base.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The report recommends a range of guiding principles to prevent <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">compulsory sterilization</a> in medical treatment, including ensuring patient autonomy in decision-making, ensuring non-discrimination, accountability and access to remedies.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_rights_and_access">Youth rights and access</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Youth rights and access">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">Sex education</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minors">Minors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Minors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Parental_consent" title="Parental consent">Parental consent</a></div>
<p>In many jurisdictions minors require parental consent or parental notification in order to access various reproductive services, such as contraception, abortion, gynecological consultations,  testing for STDs etc. The requirement that minors have parental consent/notification for testing for <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> is especially controversial, particularly in areas where the disease is endemic, and it is a sensitive subject.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Balancing minors' rights versus parental rights is considered an <a href="/wiki/Ethical" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethical">ethical</a> problem in medicine and law, and there have been many court cases on this issue in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> An important concept recognized since 1989 by the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a> is that of the <a href="/wiki/Evolving_capacities" title="Evolving capacities">
evolving capacities of a minor</a>, namely that minors should, in accordance with their maturity and level of understanding, be involved in decisions that affect them.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Youth" title="Youth">Youth</a> are often denied equal access to reproductive health services because <a href="/wiki/Health_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Health workers">health workers</a> view adolescent sexual activity as unacceptable,<sup id="cite_ref-Mugisha_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mugisha-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> or see sex education as the responsibility of parents.  Providers of reproductive health have little accountability to youth clients, a primary factor in denying youth access to reproductive health care.<sup id="cite_ref-Mugisha_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mugisha-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In many countries, regardless of legislation, minors are denied even the most basic reproductive care, if they are not accompanied by parents: in India, for instance, in 2017, a 17-year-old girl who was rejected by her family due to her pregnancy, was also rejected by hospitals and gave birth in the street.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In recent years the lack of reproductive rights for adolescents has been a concern of international organizations, such as <a href="/wiki/UNFPA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFPA">UNFPA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mandatory involvement of parents in cases where the minor has sufficient maturity to understand their situation is considered by health organization as a violation of minor's rights and detrimental to their heath. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> has criticized parental consent/notification laws:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Discrimination in health care settings takes many forms and is often manifested when an individual or group is denied access to health care services that are otherwise available to others. It can also occur through denial of services that are only needed by certain groups, such as women. Examples include specific individuals or groups being subjected to physical and verbal abuse or violence; involuntary treatment; <b>breaches of confidentiality and/or denial of autonomous decision-making, such as the requirement of consent to treatment by parents, spouses or guardians</b>; and lack of free and informed consent. [...] Laws and policies must respect the principles of autonomy in health care decision-making; guarantee free and informed consent, privacy and confidentiality; prohibit mandatory HIV testing; prohibit screening procedures that are not of benefit to the individual or the public; and ban involuntary treatment and <b>mandatory third-party authorization and notification requirements</b>."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>According to UNICEF: "When dealing with sexual and reproductive health, the obligation
to inform parents and obtain their consent becomes a significant barrier with consequences for adolescents’ lives and for public health in general."<sup id="cite_ref-UnicefBAJA_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnicefBAJA-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> One specific issue which is seen as a form of hypocrisy of legislators is that of having a higher age of medical consent for the purpose of reproductive and sexual health than the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_sexual_consent" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of sexual consent">age of sexual consent</a> - in such cases the law allows youth to engage in sexual activity, but does not allow them to consent to medical procedures that may arise from being sexually active; UNICEF states that "On sexual and reproductive health matters, the minimum age of medical consent should never be higher than the age of sexual consent."<sup id="cite_ref-UnicefBAJA_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnicefBAJA-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in Africa">HIV/AIDS in Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg/220px-Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg/330px-Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg/440px-Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ian_Mackenzie_High_School_Classroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A classroom in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg/220px-No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg/330px-No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg/440px-No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:No_Sex_Signage_in_Ghana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ad promoting abstinence in <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>: <i>No Sex Ad</i> (Anti-<a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> ― <a href="/wiki/Signage" title="Signage">signage</a>). <a href="/wiki/Abstinence-only_sex_education" title="Abstinence-only sex education">Abstinence-only sex education</a> is a form of <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> that teaches <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abstinence" title="Sexual abstinence">not having sex</a> outside of marriage, most often excluding other types of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_and_reproductive_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual and reproductive health">sexual and reproductive health</a> education, such as <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">safe sex</a>. <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Sex_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive Sex Education">Comprehensive sex education</a>, by contrast, covers the use of birth control and sexual abstinence.</div></div></div>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancies" class="mw-redirect" title="Unintended pregnancies">unintended pregnancies</a> stem from traditional contraceptive methods or no <a href="/wiki/Contraceptive" class="mw-redirect" title="Contraceptive">contraceptive</a> measures.<sup id="cite_ref-Lukale_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lukale-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Youth sexual education in Uganda is relatively low.  <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_sex_education" title="Comprehensive sex education">Comprehensive sex education</a> is not generally taught in schools; even if it was, the majority of young people do not stay in school after the age of fifteen, so information would be limited regardless.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> experiences high rates of unintended pregnancy, along with high rates of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.  Young women aged 15–24 are eight times more likely to have HIV/AIDS than young men. <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> is the world region most affected by HIV/AIDS, with approximately 25 million people living with HIV in 2015. Sub-Saharan Africa accounts for two-thirds of the global total of new HIV infections.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Attempted <a href="/wiki/Abortions" class="mw-redirect" title="Abortions">abortions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortions" class="mw-redirect" title="Unsafe abortions">unsafe abortions</a> are a risk for youth in Africa.  On average, there are 2.4 million unsafe abortions in East Africa, 1.8 million in Western Africa, over 900,000 in Middle Africa, and over 100,000 in Southern Africa each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Lukale_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lukale-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, abortion is illegal except to save the mother's life.  However, 78% of teenagers report knowing someone who has had an abortion and the police do not always prosecute everyone who has an abortion.  An estimated 22% of all <a href="/wiki/Maternal_deaths" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal deaths">maternal deaths</a> in the area stem from illegal, unsafe abortions.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Over 85% of European women (all ages) have used some form of <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> in their lives.<sup id="cite_ref-Irala_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irala-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  Europeans as an aggregate report using <a href="/wiki/Oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Oral contraceptive pill">the pill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Condoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Condoms">condoms</a> as the most commonly used contraceptives.<sup id="cite_ref-Irala_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irala-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">Family planning</a> has become prominent throughout the region and most taboos concerning sexuality have been lifted or diminished.<sup id="cite_ref-Ketting_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ketting-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>  Youth sexual and reproductive health centers have been established across most of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Ketting_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ketting-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>  In <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, approximately 80% of girls and 17% of boys have visited these youth centers, which provide all or nearly all services youth need at little to no charge.<sup id="cite_ref-Ketting_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ketting-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>  Sweden has the highest percentage of lifetime contraceptive use, with 96% of its inhabitants claiming to have used birth control at some point in their life.<sup id="cite_ref-Irala_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irala-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Sweden also has a high self-reported rate of <a href="/wiki/Emergency_contraception" title="Emergency contraception">postcoital pill use</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Irala_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irala-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  A 2007 anonymous survey of Swedish 18-year-olds showed that three out of four youth were sexually active, with 5% reporting having had an <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a> and 4% reporting the contraction of an <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexually transmitted disease">STI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Larsson_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larsson-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Similar centers exist in <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ketting_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ketting-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Views on sexual practice vary throughout the region.  For example, in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (UK), sex among youth is generally looked down upon and seen as a problem in need of solution.  In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, sex between youth is viewed as normal and therefore not discussed in terms of solutions, but rather in terms of ensuring safe practices.  That being said, the UK tends to focus on stopping sexual behavior, while the Netherlands focuses on building self-esteem and healthy relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-Ketting_61-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ketting-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights_in_Latin_America" title="Reproductive rights in Latin America">Reproductive rights in Latin America</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> has come to international attention due to its harsh anti-abortion laws. Latin America is home to some of the few countries of the world with a complete ban on abortion, without an exception for saving <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChileCourt_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChileCourt-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In some of these countries, particularity in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, the enforcement of such laws is very aggressive: <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_El_Salvador" title="Abortion in El Salvador">El Salvador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Nicaragua" title="Abortion in Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> have drawn international attention for strong enforcement of their complete bans on abortion. In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Chile" title="Abortion in Chile">Chile</a> relaxed its total ban, allowing abortion to be performed when the woman’s life is in danger, when a fetus is unviable, or in cases of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, education and class play a large role in the definition of which young women become pregnant and which do not - 50% of young women who are illiterate get pregnant, compared to 11% of girls with secondary education.  The same is true for poorer individuals - 28% become impregnated while only 11% of young women in wealthier households do.  Furthermore, access to reproductive rights, including contraceptives, are limited, due to age and the perception of female morality.  Health care providers often discuss contraception theoretically, not as a device to be used on a regular basis.  Decisions concerning sexual activity often involve secrecy and taboos, as well as a lack of access to accurate information.  Even more telling, young women have much easier access to maternal healthcare than they do to contraceptive help, which helps explain high pregnancy rates in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Goicolea_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goicolea-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rates of <a href="/wiki/Adolescent_pregnancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Adolescent pregnancy">adolescent pregnancy</a> in Latin America number over a million each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Goicolea_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goicolea-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jordan">Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, there is essentially no sex education in the school system; even when curriculum includes information about sexual issues, teachers are apt to skim over it, for fear of upsetting parents or being uncomfortable.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  Youth in the country desire comprehensive, correct, and precise information from healthcare providers, although they rarely report experiencing that.  Many youth equate reproductive health with <a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">maternal health</a>, not recognizing the connections to themselves before <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Khalaf_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khalaf-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Accessibility and availability of clinics in Jordan vary depending on location.  Some villagers have a hard time making it to clinics, due to the high cost of transportation and the distance that must be covered.  Health care centers are often overcrowded and understaffed, with limited hours of operation.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  Youth report long wait times and unhygienic conditions at clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-Khalaf_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khalaf-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>  Personal experiences with health care workers vary, with some youth feeling as though they received disrespectful and unfair treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-Khalaf_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khalaf-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Birth_control_in_the_United_States" title="Birth control in the United States">Birth control in the United States</a></div>
<p>Among sexually experienced teenagers, 78% of teenage females and 85% of teenage males used contraception the first time they had sex; 86% and 93% of these same females and males, respectively, reported using contraception the last time they had sex.<sup id="cite_ref-Fact_Sheet_Guttmacher_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact_Sheet_Guttmacher-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  The male <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condom</a> is the most commonly used method during first sex, although 54% of young women in the United States rely upon the <a href="/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Combined oral contraceptive pill">pill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fact_Sheet_Guttmacher_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact_Sheet_Guttmacher-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Young people in the U.S. are no more sexually active than individuals in other developed countries, but they are significantly less knowledgeable about contraception and safe sex practices.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> As of 2006, only twenty states required <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> in schools - of these, only ten required information about contraception.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  On the whole, less than 10% of American students receive sex education that includes topical coverage of <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intimate_relationships" class="mw-redirect" title="Intimate relationships">relationships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, and STI prevention.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Abstinence-only_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Abstinence-only education">Abstinence-only education</a> was used throughout much of the United States in the 1990s and early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  Based upon the moral principle that sex outside of marriage is unacceptable, the programs often misled students about their rights to have sex, the consequences, and prevention of pregnancy and STIs.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to 2006 statistics, one in three people in the U.S. will contract an STI by the age of 24 and by the age of 20, forty percent of women have been pregnant.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  According to the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Disease_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Center for Disease Control">Center for Disease Control</a>, young people ages 15–24 account for 50% of all new STIs, the most prevalent being <a href="/wiki/HPV" class="mw-redirect" title="HPV">HPV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chlamydia_infection" title="Chlamydia infection">chlamydia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CDC_Fact_Sheet_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_Fact_Sheet-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">Family planning</a> in the United States can be expensive and often not covered by insurance plans.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudson_58-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudson-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  However, effective beginning September 23, 2010, following the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Affordable_Care_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Affordable Care Act">Affordable Care Act</a>, preventative services, including contraception, and STI screenings and counseling, are available to all insured women with no co-pay.<sup id="cite_ref-Government_Coverage_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Government_Coverage-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 24 states, legislation was passed that required women who were seeking an abortion to have an ultrasound at least 24 hours before it.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the ultrasound requirement, several states such as Texas have passed legislation requiring facilities that provide abortions to be classified as ambulatory surgery centers, despite the very low rates of abortion complications each year.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Many people view this type of legislation as a way to discourage women from getting abortions.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. Supreme Court has struck down Texas’ most recent law that would have reduced the number of facilities able to give abortions to only eight in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lack_of_knowledge_about_rights">Lack of knowledge about rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lack of knowledge about rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One of the reasons why reproductive rights are poor in many places, is that the vast majority of the population does not know what the law is. Not only are ordinary people uninformed, but so are medical doctors. A study in Brazil on medical doctors found considerable ignorance and misunderstanding of the law on abortion (which is severely restricted, but not completely illegal).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In Ghana, abortion, while restricted, is permitted on several grounds, but only 3% of pregnant women and 6% of those seeking an abortion were aware of the legal status of abortion.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In Nepal, abortion was legalized in 2002, but a study in 2009 found that only half of women knew that abortion was legalized.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Many people also do not understand the laws on <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a>: in Hungary, where <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape" title="Marital rape">marital rape</a> was made illegal in 1997, in a study in 2006, 62% of people did not know that marital rape was a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The United Nations Development Programme states that, in order to advance gender justice, "Women must know their rights and be able to access legal systems",<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and the 1993 UN Declaration on the Elimination of Violence Against Women states at Art. 4 (d) [...] "States should also inform women of their rights in seeking redress through such mechanisms".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_equality_and_violence_against_women">Gender equality and violence against women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Gender equality and violence against women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">Gender equality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">Violence against women</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">Sexual violence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">Forced marriage</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">Child marriage</a></div>
<p>Addressing issues of gender-based violence is crucial for attaining reproductive rights. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> refers to "<i><b>Equality and equity for men and women</b>, to enable individuals to make free and informed choices in all spheres of life, free from discrimination based on gender</i>" and "<i>Sexual and reproductive security, <b>including freedom from sexual violence and coercion</b>, and the right to privacy,</i>" as part of achieving reproductive rights,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and states that the <b>right to liberty and security of the person</b> which is fundamental to reproductive rights obliges states to:<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Take measures to prevent, punish and eradicate all forms of gender-based violence</li>
<li>Eliminate female genital mutilation/cutting</li></ul>
<p>The WHO states:<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>"Gender and Reproductive Rights (GRR) aims to promote and protect human rights and gender equality as they relate to sexual and reproductive health by developing strategies and mechanisms for promoting gender equity and equality and human rights in the Departments global and national activities, as well as within the functioning and priority-setting of the Department itself."</dd></dl>
<p>Amnesty International writes that:<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>Violence against women violates women's rights to life, physical and mental integrity, to the highest attainable standard of health, to freedom from torture and it violates their sexual and reproductive rights."</dd></dl>
<p>One key issue for achieving reproductive rights is criminalization of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a>.
