If a woman is not protected from forced sexual intercourse, she is not protected from <a href="/wiki/Forced_pregnancy" title="Forced pregnancy">forced pregnancy</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_from_rape" title="Pregnancy from rape">pregnancy from rape</a>. In order for a woman to be able to have reproductive rights, she must have the right to choose with whom and when to reproduce; and first of all, decide whether, when, and under what circumstances to be sexually active.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In many countries, these rights of women are not respected, because women do not have a choice in regard to their partner, with <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">child marriage</a> being common in parts of the world; and neither do they have any rights in regard to sexual activity, as many countries do not allow women to refuse to engage in sexual intercourse when they do not want to (because <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape" title="Marital rape">marital rape</a> is not criminalized in those countries) or to engage in consensual sexual intercourse if they want to (because sex outside marriage is illegal in those countries). In addition to legal barriers, there are also social barriers, because in many countries a complete sexual subordination of a woman to her husband is expected (for instance, in one survey 74% of women in Mali said that a husband is justified to beat his wife if she refuses to have sex with him<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>), while sexual/romantic relations disapproved by family members, or generally sex outside marriage, can result in serious violence, such as <a href="/wiki/Honor_killings" class="mw-redirect" title="Honor killings">honor killings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="HIV.2FAIDS"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg" class="image"><img alt="A map of the world where most of the land is colored green or yellow except for sub Saharan Africa which is colored red" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg/260px-AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg.png" width="260" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg/390px-AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg/520px-AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="477" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AIDS_and_HIV_prevalence_2008.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estimated <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> in&#160;% of HIV among young adults (15–49) per country as of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  <div>  &#32; <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #787878; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>No data</small></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #94bf8b; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>&lt;0.10</small></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f4e2ba; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>0.10–0.5</small></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #eaca83; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>0.5–1</small></div> &#32; </td> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f07568; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>1–5</small></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff4800; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>5–15</small></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b00000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<small>15–50</small></div> &#32; </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div></div>
<p>According to the CDC, "HIV stands for human immunodeficiency virus. It weakens a person’s immune system by destroying important cells that fight disease and infection. No effective cure exists for HIV. But with proper medical care, HIV can be controlled."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  HIV amelioration is an important aspect of reproductive rights because the virus can be transmitted from mother to child during pregnancy or birth, or via breast milk.
</p><p>The WHO states that: "All women, including those with HIV, have the right “to decide freely and responsibly on the number and spacing of their children and to have access to the information, education and means to enable them to exercise these rights”".<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The reproductive rights of people living with HIV, and their health, are very important. The link between HIV and reproductive rights exists in regard to four main issues:<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>prevention of unwanted pregnancy</li>
<li>help to plan wanted pregnancy</li>
<li>healthcare during and after pregnancy</li>
<li>access to abortion services</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_and_forced_marriage">Child and forced marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Child and forced marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">Child marriage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">Forced marriage</a></div>
<p>The WHO states that the reproductive rights and health of girls in child marriages are negatively affected.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">UNPF</a> calls child marriage a "human rights violation" and states that in developing countries, one in every three girls is married before reaching age 18, and one in nine is married under age 15.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a> is a marriage in which one or more of the parties is married without his or her consent or against his or her will. The <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_preventing_and_combating_violence_against_women_and_domestic_violence" title="Convention on preventing and combating violence against women and domestic violence">Istanbul convention</a>, the first legally binding instrument in Europe in the field of violence against women and domestic violence,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> requires countries which ratify it to prohibit <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a> (Article 37) and to ensure that forced marriages can be easily voided without further victimization (Article 32).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maternal_mortality">Maternal mortality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Maternal mortality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">Maternal death</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg/300px-Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg" width="300" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg/450px-Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg/600px-Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="820" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maternal_mortality_rate_worldwide.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maternal_Mortality_Rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal Mortality Rate">Maternal Mortality Rate</a> worldwide, as defined by the number of maternal deaths per 100,000 live births from any cause related to or aggravated by pregnancy or its management, excluding accidental or incidental causes.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA2010_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA2010-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Maternal death is defined by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) as "the death of a woman while pregnant or within 42 days of termination of <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, irrespective of the duration and site of the pregnancy, from any cause related to or aggravated by the pregnancy or its management but not from accidental or incidental causes."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It is estimated that in 2015, about 303,000 women died during and following pregnancy and childbirth, and 99% of such deaths occur in developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_Programme_of_Action_implementation">Cairo Programme of Action implementation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cairo Programme of Action implementation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Implementation of the Cairo Programme of Action varies considerably from country to country. In many countries, post-ICPD tensions emerged as the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>-based approach was implemented. Since the ICPD, many countries have broadened their reproductive health programs and attempted to integrate maternal and child health services with family planning. More attention is paid to adolescent health and the consequences of unsafe abortion. Lara Knudsen observes that the ICPD succeeded in getting <a href="/wiki/Feminist" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist">feminist</a> language into governments' and population agencies' literature, but in many countries the underlying concepts are not widely put into practice.<sup id="cite_ref-Knudsen_2006_7_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knudsen_2006_7-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In two preparatory meetings for the ICPD+10 in Asia and Latin America, the United States, under the George W. Bush Administration, was the only nation opposing the ICPD's Programme of Action.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion">Abortion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Abortion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Abortion_law" title="Abortion law">Abortion law</a></div>
<p>According to a study by WHO and the Guttmacher Institute worldwide, 25 million <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">unsafe abortions</a> (45% of all abortions) occurred every year between 2010 and 2014. 97% of unsafe abortions occur in developing countries in Africa, Asia and Latin America. By contrast, most abortions that take place in Western and Northern Europe and North America are safe.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_the_Elimination_of_Discrimination_against_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee on the Elimination of Discrimination against Women">Committee on the Elimination of Discrimination against Women</a> considers the criminalization of abortion a "violations of women’s sexual and reproductive health and rights" and a form of "gender based violence"; paragraph 18 of its <i>General recommendation No. 35 on gender based violence against women, updating general recommendation No. 19</i> states that: "Violations of women’s sexual and reproductive health and rights, such as forced sterilizations, forced abortion, forced pregnancy, criminalisation of abortion, denial or delay of  safe  abortion  and  post abortion  care,  forced  continuation  of pregnancy,  abuse  and mistreatment  of  women  and  girls  seeking  sexual  and  reproductive  health  information, goods and services, are forms of <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">gender based violence</a> that, depending on   the circumstances, may amount to torture or cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment."<sup id="cite_ref-tbinternet.ohchr.org_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbinternet.ohchr.org-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The same <i>General Recommendation</i> also urges countries at paragraph 31 to [...] In particular, repeal:
a) Provisions  that  allow,  tolerate  or  condone  forms  of  gender based  violence against women, including [...] legislation  that  criminalises  abortion".<sup id="cite_ref-tbinternet.ohchr.org_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbinternet.ohchr.org-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An article from the World Health Organization calls safe, legal abortion a "<a href="/wiki/Fundamental_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamental right">fundamental right</a> of women, irrespective of where they live" and <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">unsafe abortion</a> a "silent <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The article states "ending the silent pandemic of unsafe abortion is an urgent <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public-health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human-rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Human-rights">human-rights</a> imperative." It also states "access to safe abortion improves <a href="/wiki/Women%E2%80%99s_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Women’s health">women’s health</a>, and vice versa, as documented in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> during the regime of President <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>" and "legalisation of abortion on request is a necessary but insufficient step toward improving women’s health" citing that in some countries, such as India where abortion has been legal for decades, access to competent care remains restricted because of other barriers. WHO’s Global Strategy on Reproductive Health, adopted by the World Health Assembly in May 2004, noted: “As a preventable cause of maternal mortality and morbidity, unsafe abortion must be dealt with as part of the MDG on improving maternal health and other international development goals and targets." <sup id="cite_ref-who.int_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The WHO's Development and Research Training in Human Reproduction (HRP), whose research concerns people's sexual and reproductive health and lives,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> has an overall strategy to combat unsafe abortion that comprises four inter-related activities:<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>to collate, synthesize and generate scientifically sound evidence on unsafe abortion prevalence and practices;</li>
<li>to develop improved technologies and implement interventions to make abortion safer;</li>
<li>to translate evidence into norms, tools and guidelines;</li>
<li>and to assist in the development of programmes and policies that reduce unsafe abortion and improve access to safe abortion and highquality postabortion care</li></ul>
<p>The UN has estimated in 2017 that repealing anti-abortion laws would save the lives of nearly 50,000 women a year.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Unsafe abortions take place primarily in countries where abortion is illegal, but also occur in countries where it is legal, but women cannot access it because of various reasons (<a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objectors</a> among doctors, high prices, lack of knowledge that abortion is legal). Indeed, there are countries where the law  is liberal, but in practice it is very difficult to have an abortion, due to most doctors being  conscientious objectors.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The fact that is some countries where abortion is legal it is <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> very difficult to have access to one is controversial; the UN in its 2017 resolution on <i>Intensification of efforts to prevent and eliminate all forms of violence against women and girls: domestic violence</i> urged states to guarantee access to "safe abortion where such services are permitted by national law".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Safe and legal abortion services are often very difficult to access by women from rural areas or from lower socioeconomic backgrounds. In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> stated that "In fact, even where abortion is permitted by law, women often have severely limited access to safe abortion services because of lack of proper regulation, health services, or political will" and estimated that "Approximately 13 percent of maternal deaths worldwide are attributable to unsafe abortion—between 68,000 and 78,000 deaths annually."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When negotiating the Cairo Programme of Action at the 1994 <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_on_Population_and_Development" title="International Conference on Population and Development">International Conference on Population and Development</a> (ICPD), the issue was so contentious that delegates eventually decided to omit any recommendation to legalize abortion, instead advising governments to provide proper post-abortion care and to invest in programs that will decrease the number of unwanted pregnancies.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 18, 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</a>, a group comprising members from 47 European countries, adopted a resolution calling for the decriminalization of abortion within reasonable gestational limits and guaranteed access to safe abortion procedures. The nonbinding resolution was passed on April 16 by a vote of 102 to 69.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During and after the ICPD, some interested parties attempted to interpret the term ‘reproductive health’ in the sense that it implies abortion as a means of family planning or, indeed, a right to abortion. These interpretations, however, do not reflect the consensus reached at the Conference.
For the European Union, where legislation on abortion is certainly less restrictive than elsewhere, the Council Presidency has clearly stated that the Council’s commitment to promote ‘reproductive health’ did not include the promotion of abortion.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>  Likewise, the European Commission, in response to a question from a Member of the European Parliament, clarified:
</p><p><i>“The term ‘reproductive health’ was defined by the United Nations (UN) in 1994 at the Cairo International Conference on Population and Development. All Member States of the Union endorsed the Programme of Action adopted at Cairo. The Union has never adopted an alternative definition of ‘reproductive health’ to that given in the Programme of Action, <b>which makes no reference to abortion</b>.”</i><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With regard to the U.S., it should be noted that, only a few days prior to the Cairo Conference, the head of the U.S. delegation, Vice President Al Gore, had stated for the record:
</p><p><i>“Let us get a false issue off the table: the US does not seek to establish a new international right to abortion, and we do not believe that abortion should be encouraged as a method of family planning.”</i><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some years later, the position of the U.S. Administration in this debate was reconfirmed by U.S. Ambassador to the UN, Ellen Sauerbrey, when she stated at a meeting of the UN Commission on the Status of Women that: <i>“nongovernmental organizations are attempting to assert that Beijing  in some way creates or contributes to the creation of an internationally recognized fundamental right to abortion”</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> She added: <i>“There is no fundamental right to abortion. And yet it keeps coming up largely driven by NGOs trying to hijack the term and trying to make it into a definition”</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Collaborative research from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Development_Studies" title="Institute of Development Studies">Institute of Development Studies</a> states that "access to safe abortion is a matter of human rights, democracy and public health, and the denial of such access is a major cause of death and impairment, with significant costs to [international] development".<sup id="cite_ref-IDS2009_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDS2009-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The research highlights the inequities of access to safe abortion both globally and nationally and emphasises the importance of global and national movements for reform to address this. The shift by campaigners of reproductive rights from an issue-based agenda (the right to abortion), to safe, legal abortion not only as a human right, but bound up with democratic and citizenship rights, has been an important way of reframing the abortion debate and reproductive justice agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-IDS2009_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDS2009-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> complicated the question even more through a landmark judgment (case of <i><a href="/wiki/A._B._and_C._v._Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="A. B. and C. v. Ireland">A. B. and C. v. Ireland</a></i>), in which it is stated that the denial of abortion for health and/or well-being reasons is an interference with an individuals right to respect for private and family life under Article 8 of the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>, an interference which in some cases can be justified.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_control">Population control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Population control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Population_control" title="Population control">Population control</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg/250px-Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg" width="250" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg/375px-Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg/500px-Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1267" data-file-height="890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceausescu_Anul_Nou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>, Romanian communist leader, enacted one of the most infamous <a href="/wiki/Natalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Natalist">natalist</a> policies of the 20th century</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg/250px-Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg/375px-Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg/500px-Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Danshan_Nongguang_Village_Bulletin_board.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A community bulletin board in Nonguang Village, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Sichuan province">Sichuan province</a>, China, keeping track of the town's female population, listing recent births by name and noting that several thousand yuan of fines for unauthorized births remain unpaid from the previous year.</div></div></div>
<p>A desire to achieve certain population targets has resulted throughout history in severely abusive practices, in cases where governments ignored human rights and enacted aggressive demographic policies. In the 20th century, several authoritarian governments have sought either to increase or to decrease the births rates, often through forceful intervention. One of the most notorious <a href="/wiki/Natalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Natalist">natalist</a> policies is that which occurred in <a href="/wiki/Communist_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Romania">communist Romania</a> in the period of 1967-1990 during communist leader <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>, who adopted a very aggressive natalist policy which included outlawing abortion and contraception, routine pregnancy tests for women, <a href="/wiki/Tax_on_childlessness" title="Tax on childlessness">taxes on childlessness</a>, and legal discrimination against childless people.  Ceaușescu's policy resulted in over 9,000 women who died due to <a href="/wiki/Illegal_abortion" title="Illegal abortion">illegal abortions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kligman_short_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kligman_short-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> large numbers of children put into <a href="/wiki/Romanian_orphanages" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian orphanages">Romanian orphanages</a> by parents who couldn't cope with raising them, <a href="/wiki/Street_children" title="Street children">street children</a> in the 1990s (when many orphanages were closed and the children ended on the streets), and <a href="/wiki/Overcrowding" title="Overcrowding">overcrowding</a> in homes and schools. The irony of Ceaușescu's aggressive natalist policy was a generation that may not have been born would eventually lead the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution" title="Romanian Revolution">Romanian Revolution</a> which would overthrow and have him <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Nicolae_and_Elena_Ceau%C8%99escu#Execution" title="Trial of Nicolae and Elena Ceaușescu">executed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In stark opposition with Ceaușescu's natalist policy was China's <a href="/wiki/One_child_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="One child policy">one child policy</a>, in effect from 1978 to 2015, which included abuses such as <a href="/wiki/Forced_abortion" title="Forced abortion">forced abortions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> This policy has also been deemed responsible for the common practice of <a href="/wiki/Sex_selective_abortion" class="mw-redirect" title="Sex selective abortion">sex selective abortion</a> which led to an imbalanced <a href="/wiki/Sex_ratio" title="Sex ratio">sex ratio</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Bulte,_Heerink,_&amp;_Zhang,_2011_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bulte,_Heerink,_&amp;_Zhang,_2011-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From the 1970s to 1980s, tension grew between women's health activists who advance women's reproductive rights as part of a human rights-based approach on the one hand, and population control advocates on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> At the 1984 UN World Population Conference in Mexico City population control policies came under attack from women's health advocates who argued that the policies' narrow focus led to coercion and decreased quality of care, and that these policies ignored the varied social and cultural contexts in which family planning was provided in developing countries. In the 1980s the HIV/AIDS epidemic forced a broader discussion of sex into the public discourse in many countries, leading to more emphasis on reproductive health issues beyond reducing fertility. The growing opposition to the narrow population control focus led to a significant departure in the early 1990s from past population control policies.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>  In the United States, abortion opponents have begun to foment <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theories</a> about reproductive rights advocates, accusing them of advancing a <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racist</a> agenda of <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a>, and of trying to reduce the <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> birth rate in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-Dewan_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dewan-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Female_genital_mutilation">Female genital mutilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Female genital mutilation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg/200px-FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg.png" width="200" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg/300px-FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg/400px-FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1548" data-file-height="1248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FGM_prevalence_UNICEF_2016.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prevalence of FGM</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM) is defined as "all procedures that involve partial or total removal of the external female genitalia, or other injury to the female genital organs for non-medical reasons."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The procedure has no health benefits, and can cause severe bleeding and problems urinating, cysts, infections, and complications in childbirth and increased risk of newborn deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> It is performed for traditional, cultural or religious reasons in many parts of the world, especially in Africa. The <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_preventing_and_combating_violence_against_women_and_domestic_violence" title="Convention on preventing and combating violence against women and domestic violence">Istanbul Convention</a> prohibits FGM (Article 38).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bride_kidnapping_or_buying_and_reproductive_slavery">Bride kidnapping or buying and reproductive slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bride kidnapping or buying and reproductive slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg/220px-Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg/330px-Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg/440px-Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1353" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_rugendas_-_el_malon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The painting depicts a Chilean woman being kidnapped during a <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%B3n" title="Malón">malón</a>.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bride_kidnapping" title="Bride kidnapping">Bride kidnapping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">Bride price</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bride_kidnapping" title="Bride kidnapping">Bride kidnapping</a> or marriage by abduction, is the practice whereby a woman or girl is abducted for the purpose of a <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a>. Bride kidnapping has been practiced historically in many parts of the world, and it continues to occur today in some places, especially in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, in countries such as  Kyrgyzstan, Tajikistan, Kazakhstan, Turkmenistan, Uzbekistan and Armenia, as well as in Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Bride kidnapping is often preceded or followed by rape (which may result in pregnancy), in order to force the marriage - a practice also supported by "<a href="/wiki/Marry-your-rapist_law" title="Marry-your-rapist law">marry-your-rapist law</a>" (laws regarding sexual violence, abduction or similar acts, whereby the perpetrator avoids prosecution or punishment if he marries the victim<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>). Abducting of women may happen on an individual scale or on a mass scale. <a href="/wiki/Raptio" title="Raptio">Raptio</a> is a Latin term referring to the large-scale abduction of women, usually for marriage or sexual slavery, particularity during wartime.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">Bride price</a>, also called bridewealth, is money, property, or other form of wealth paid by a groom or his family to the parents of the woman he marries. The practice of bride price sometimes leads to parents selling young daughters into marriage and to trafficking.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>Bride price is common across Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Such forced marriages often lead to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forced_pregnancy" title="Forced pregnancy">forced pregnancy</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ghana" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ghana">northern Ghana</a>, for example, the payment of bride price signifies a woman's requirement to bear children, and women using birth control are at risks of threats and coercion.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1956 <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_Convention_on_the_Abolition_of_Slavery,_the_Slave_Trade,_and_Institutions_and_Practices_Similar_to_Slavery" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplementary Convention on the Abolition of Slavery, the Slave Trade, and Institutions and Practices Similar to Slavery">Supplementary Convention on the Abolition of Slavery, the Slave Trade, and Institutions and Practices Similar to Slavery</a> defines "institutions and practices similar to slavery" to include:<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>c) Any institution or practice whereby:
</p>
<ul><li>(i) A woman, without the right to refuse, is promised or given in marriage on payment of a consideration in money or in kind to her parents, guardian, family or any other person or group; or</li>
<li>(ii) The husband of a woman, his family, or his clan, has the right to transfer her to another person for value received or otherwise; or</li>
<li>(iii) A woman on the death of her husband is liable to be inherited by another person;</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sperm_donation">Sperm donation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sperm donation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sperm_donation" title="Sperm donation">Sperm donation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sperm_donor_limitation_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Sperm donor limitation by country">Sperm donor limitation by country</a></div>
<p>Laws in many countries and states require <a href="/wiki/Sperm_donation" title="Sperm donation">sperm donors</a> to be either anonymous or known to the recipient, or the laws restrict the number of children each donor may father. Although many donors choose to remain anonymous, new <a href="/wiki/Technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Technologies">technologies</a> such as the Internet and DNA technology have opened up new avenues for those wishing to know more about the biological father, siblings and half-siblings.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compulsory_sterilization">Compulsory sterilization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Compulsory sterilization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg/250px-SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg" width="250" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg/375px-SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg/500px-SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3039" data-file-height="1887" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SOU_1929_14_Bet%C3%A4nkande_med_f%C3%B6rslag_till_steriliseringslag_s_57_Laughlin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map from a 1929 Swedish royal commission report displays the U.S. states that had implemented sterilization legislation by then</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">Compulsory sterilization</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_castration" title="Chemical castration">Chemical castration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">Eugenics</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roma_women">Roma women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Roma women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Roma_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma people">Roma people</a></div>
<p>During the 20th century, forced sterilization of <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> women in European countries, especially in former Communist countries, was practiced,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and there are allegations that these practices continue unofficially in some countries, such as Czech Republic, Bulgaria, Hungary and Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/V._C._vs._Slovakia" title="V. C. vs. Slovakia">V. C. vs. Slovakia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="European Court for Human Rights">European Court for Human Rights</a> ruled in favor of a Roma woman who was the victim of forced sterilization in a state hospital in <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_2">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>An individual’s sterilization is one of the main issues behind the reproductive rights that are being ignored by those who believe that they have a right to decide whether certain people are "fit" to have children. The mental stability of an individual and the physical defects that an individual might have played an important role in the beginnings of forced sterilization. Individuals were afraid that these defects were hereditary and wanted to put a stop to it before society became incompetent. Although there are numerous operations which may render one sterile, <a href="/wiki/Vasectomy" title="Vasectomy">vasectomy</a> in the male and <a href="/wiki/Salpingectomy" title="Salpingectomy">salpingectomy</a> in the female are considered the least radical. Neither operation is considered dangerous.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>  The laws of the states in which sterilization is practiced vary. Numerous provisions have been made both by the United States and by individual states for limiting the number of degenerates in this country. The creation of voluntary programs such as <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood" title="Planned Parenthood">Planned Parenthood</a> (presented the use of <a href="/wiki/Abstinence" title="Abstinence">abstinence</a> and contraceptives as forms of controlling the population growth) were introduced to help families control their birth rate.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sterilization has long been a controversial topic in the United States. Up through the 1970s, states could choose which women were allowed the procedure and which women were not eligible. This strategy proved repressive, both for women who wished to become sterilized and were not granted the right, as well as for women who had no choice but to become sterilized<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2014)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Then, as today, sterilization was a form of birth control highly sought after by some women. However, until the 1960s, it was illegal for women to become sterilized for reasons other than eugenics, which meant sterilization as birth control was illegal. This left many women with highly legitimate reasons for sterilization unable to receive the procedure. It also meant most women who were undergoing the procedure were getting it for non-birth control reasons and not by choice.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, both compulsory and coercive sterilization have become constitutional issues because some argue that it violates an individual’s ‘right to procreate’. In 1972, <i><a href="/wiki/Eisenstadt_v._Baird" title="Eisenstadt v. Baird">Eisenstadt v. Baird</a></i> set the precedent: “the right of the individual, married or single, to be free from unwarranted government intrusion into matters so fundamentally affecting a person as the decision to bear or beget a child”. Yet, sterilization is still being used in court sentencing for both men and women in cases involving child abuse and/or neglect, drug abuse, and other criminal activity. The relationship between reproductive rights and sterilization is also visible in hospital settings where doctors have been documented as ordering women, namely low-income women of color, to consent to sterilization or have their birthing services withheld.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Canada recently took the initiative in assisting women seeking abortions globally, as on Wednesday March 8, 2017, International Women's Day, Prime Minister Justin Trudeau announced a $650 million advocacy program.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The move came following the United States of America cutting its budget for reproductive Health and Family Planning in the developing world. Under the previous Obama Government, the United States had pause a policy that withheld funding for abortions and sexual health resources globally.<sup id="cite_ref-CBC02032017_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBC02032017-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> However, under the Trump administration, the policy was reinitiated, as it had been under previous Republican governments.<sup id="cite_ref-CBC02032017_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBC02032017-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The program sees Canada become a worldwide leader in women’s rights initiatives, as it assists in advocacy for safe, and legal abortions in Nations that currently prohibit them.
</p><p>Abortion is currently illegal in an estimated 125 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Trudeau and the Liberal Government of Canada emphasized that this money will assist in developing support groups globally to challenge the legislation within these nations to enforce women’s rights.
</p><p>According to the Canadian Government the primary focus of the foreign aid strategy is "removing judicial and legal barriers to the fulfillment of sexual and reproductive health and rights".<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The strategy aims to reduce unsafe abortions and educate individuals on contraception and family planning.
</p><p>The move illustrated a push to assist women globally after a shift in gender lenses has become more prevalent. Advocacy groups have recently rallied to make global standards move inclusive for women in recent years, and the move by the Canadian Government only emphasized this more. International Development Minister Marie-Claude Bibeau emphasized that society needs to "apply a feminist lens", and to advocate for parity amongst genders.<sup id="cite_ref-CBC02032017_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBC02032017-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the implementation of the program holds potential to be heavily criticized globally, as nations such as Africa consist of primarily conservative governments, with heavily religious investment. Christian and Islamic groups heavily influence these governments, and are exceptionally anti-abortion under religious code.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Yearly, "21.6 million women experience a unsafe abortion worldwide", with over 18.5 million of these occurring in developing nation.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> These staggering figures led to many individuals expressing support for the new Canadian Governments plan, stating that "it comes at a critical moment, when the world is seeing the clawing back of hard-won women’s rights in many countries".<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Prime Minister Trudeau emphasized his personal support with regards to stopping the high mortality rate saying that "Far too many women and girls, unsafe abortions and lack of choices in reproductive health mean that they either are at risk of death or else simply cannot contribute and cannot achieve their full potential”"<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Internally, Canadian political parties were at odds with the nature of the policy and the allocation of funds from the budget. NDP representative Hélène Laverdière stated that her party is pleased with the initiative, but feel that the amount of money is not enough to have a major impact. Contrarily, Conservative party representative Karen Vecchio, expressed displeasure with the decision, stating that they would rather see the money invested on home soil towards Indigenous women.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe30092017_146-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe30092017-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Roman Catholic Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Latin America">Roman Catholicism in Latin America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_Central_America.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CIA_map_of_Central_America.png/220px-CIA_map_of_Central_America.png" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CIA_map_of_Central_America.png/330px-CIA_map_of_Central_America.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CIA_map_of_Central_America.png/440px-CIA_map_of_Central_America.png 2x" data-file-width="1272" data-file-height="1014" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_Central_America.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> has very strict anti-abortion laws, and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> has come to international attention due to its forceful enforcement.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> is opposed to artificial contraception, abortion, and <a href="/wiki/Premarital_sex" title="Premarital sex">sexual intercourse outside marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> This belief dates back to the first centuries of Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-therealpresence1_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-therealpresence1-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> While Roman Catholicism is not the only religion with such views, its religious doctrine is very powerful in influencing countries where most of the population is Catholic, and the few countries of the world with complete bans on abortion are Catholic-majority countries,<sup id="cite_ref-ChileCourt_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChileCourt-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and in Europe strict restrictions on abortion exist in the Catholic majority countries of <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Malta" title="Abortion in Malta">Malta</a> (complete ban), <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Abortion in the Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Andorra" title="Abortion in Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_San_Marino" title="Abortion in San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Liechtenstein" title="Abortion in Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Poland" title="Abortion in Poland">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Monaco" title="Abortion in Monaco">Monaco</a>.
</p><p>Some of the countries of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, notably <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_El_Salvador" title="Abortion in El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, have also come to international attention due to very forceful enforcement of the anti-abortion laws.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> El Salvador has received repeated criticism from the UN. The Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights (OHCHR) named the law "one of the most draconian abortion laws in the world", and urged liberalization,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Zeid_bin_Ra%27ad" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Zeid bin Ra&#39;ad">Zeid bin Ra'ad</a>, the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights, stated that he was "appalled that as a result of El Salvador’s absolute prohibition on abortion, women are being punished for apparent miscarriages and other obstetric emergencies, accused and convicted of having induced termination of pregnancy".<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reproductive_rights&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_the_legalization_of_abortion" class="mw-redirect" title="Opposition to the legalization of abortion">opponents of legalized abortion</a> view the term "reproductive rights" as a <a href="/wiki/Euphemism" title="Euphemism">euphemism</a> to sway emotions in favor of abortion.  <a href="/wiki/National_Right_to_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="National Right to Life">National Right to Life</a> has referred to "reproductive rights" as a "fudge term" and "the code word for <i>abortion</i> rights."<sup id="cite_ref-NRLC_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRLC-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-FREEDMAN-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FREEDMAN_4-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Freedman, Lynn P.; Isaacs, Stephen L. <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nocirc.org/symposia/fourth/zavales4.html">"Template"</a>. <i>Nocirc.org</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">19 August</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Nocirc.org&amp;rft.atitle=Template&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nocirc.org%2Fsymposia%2Ffourth%2Fzavales4.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AReproductive+rights" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-teheran_proc-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-teheran_proc_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-teheran_proc_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071017025912/http://www.unhchr.ch/html/menu3/b/b_tehern.htm">"Proclamation of Teheran"</a>. International Conference on Human Rights. 1968. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.unhchr.ch/html/menu3/b/b_tehern.htm">the original</a> on 2007-10-17<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2007-11-08</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Proclamation+of+Teheran&amp;rft.pub=International+Conference+on+Human+Rights&amp;rft.date=1968&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.unhchr.ch%2Fhtml%2Fmenu3%2Fb%2Fb_tehern.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AReproductive+rights" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Center for Reproductive Rights, International Legal Program, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://thomas.loc.gov">Establishing International Reproductive Rights Norms: Theory for Change</a>, US CONG. REC. 108th CONG. 1 Sess. E2534 E2547 (Rep. Smith) (Dec. 8, 2003):<blockquote><p>
We have been leaders in bringing arguments for a woman's right to choose abortion within the rubric of international human rights. However, there is no binding hard norm that recognizes women's right to terminate a pregnancy. (...) While there are hard norms prohibiting sex discrimination that apply to girl adolescents, these are problematic since they must be applied to a substantive right (i.e., the right to health) and the substantive reproductive rights of adolescents are not `hard' (yet!). There are no hard norms on age discrimination that would protect adolescents' ability to exercise their rights to reproductive health, sexual education, or reproductive decisionmaking. In addition, there are no hard norms prohibiting discrimination based on marital status, which is often an issue with respect to unmarried adolescents' access to reproductive health services and information. The soft norms support the idea that the hard norms apply to adolescents under 18. They also fill in the substantive gaps in the hard norms with respect to reproductive health services and information as well as adolescents' reproductive autonomy. (...) There are no hard norms in international human rights law that directly address HIV/AIDS directly. At the same time, a number of human rights bodies have developed soft norms to secure rights that are rendered vulnerable by the HIV/AIDS epidemic. (...) Practices with implications for women's reproductive rights in relation to HIV/AIDS are still not fully covered under existing international law, although soft norms have addressed them to some extent. (...) There is a lack of explicit prohibition of mandatory testing of HIV-positive pregnant women under international law. (...) None of the global human rights treaties explicitly prohibit child marriage and no treaty prescribes an appropriate minimum age for marriage. The onus of specifying a minimum age at marriage rests with the states' parties to these treaties. (...) We have to rely extensively on soft norms that have evolved from the TMBs and that are contained in conference documents to assert that child marriage is a violation of fundamental human rights.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Knudsen, Lara (2006). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=b3thCcdyScsC&amp;dq=reproductive+rights"><i>Reproductive Rights in a Global Context</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160708000957/https://rm.coe.int/CoERMPublicCommonSearchServices/DisplayDCTMContent?documentId=090000168046031c">"Archived copy"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://rm.coe.int/CoERMPublicCommonSearchServices/DisplayDCTMContent?documentId=090000168046031c">the original</a> on 2016-07-08<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2016-09-26</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Archived+copy&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Frm.coe.int%2FCoERMPublicCommonSearchServices%2FDisplayDCTMContent%3FdocumentId%3D090000168046031c&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AReproductive+rights" class="Z3988"></span><span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33; margin-left:0.3em">CS1 maint: Archived copy as title (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_Archived_copy_as_title" title="Category:CS1 maint: Archived copy as title">link</a>) </span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Amnesty International, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/human-rights-defenders/issues/challenges/srr-defenders">Defenders of Sexual and Reproductive Rights</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20131002004052/http://www.amnesty.org/en/human-rights-defenders/issues/challenges/srr-defenders">Archived</a> 2013-10-02 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iwhc.org/index.php?option=com_content&amp;task=view&amp;id=3326&amp;Itemid=548">International Women’s Health Coalition and the United Nations</a>,  <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iwhc.org/index.php?option=com_content&amp;task=view&amp;id=205&amp;Itemid=110">Campaign for an Inter-American Convention on Sexual and Reproductive Rights </a>, Women's Health Collection, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thefreelibrary.com/_/print/PrintArticle.aspx?id=105915323">Abortion as a human right: possible strategies in unexplored territory. (Sexual Rights and Reproductive Rights),</a> (2003); and Shanthi Dairiam, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thefreelibrary.com/_/print/PrintArticle.aspx?id=90988094">Applying the CEDAW Convention for the recognition of women's health rights</a>, Arrows For Change, (2002).  In this regard, the Center for Reproductive Rights has noted that: <blockquote><p>
Our goal is to ensure that governments worldwide guarantee women's reproductive rights out of an understanding that they are bound to do so. The two principal prerequisites for achieving this goal are: (1) the strengthening of international legal norms protecting reproductive rights; and (2) consistent and effective action on the part of civil society and the international community to enforce these norms. Each of these conditions, in turn, depends upon profound social change at the local, national and international (including regional) levels. (...) Ultimately, we must persuade governments to accept reproductive rights as binding norms. Again, our approach can move forward on several fronts, with interventions both at the national and international levels. Governments' recognition of reproductive rights norms may be indicated by their support for progressive language in international conference documents or by their adoption and implementation of appropriate national-level legislative and policy instruments. In order to counter opposition to an expansion of recognized reproductive rights norms, we have questioned the credibility of such reactionary yet influential international actors as the United States and the Holy See. Our activities to garner support for international protections of reproductive rights include: Lobbying government delegations at UN conferences and producing supporting analyses/materials; fostering alliances with members of civil society who may become influential on their national delegations to the UN; and preparing briefing papers and factsheets exposing the broad anti-woman agenda of our opposition.</p></blockquote>Center for Reproductive Rights, International Legal Program, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://thomas.loc.gov">Establishing International Reproductive Rights Norms: Theory for Change</a>, US CONG. REC. 108th CONG. 1 Sess. E2534 E2547 (Rep. Smith) (Dec. 8, 2003)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iisd.ca/Cairo/program/p07002.html">"&#91;programme&#93; Basis for action"</a>. Iisd.ca<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.un.org/popin/icpd/conference/offeng/poa.html">United Nations, Report of the Fourth International Conference on Population and Development, Cario, 5 - 13 September 1994</a>. Guatemala entered the following reservation:<blockquote><p>
Chapter VII:  we enter a reservation on the whole chapter, for the General Assembly's mandate to the Conference does not extend to the creation or formulation of rights; this reservation therefore applies to all references in the document to "reproductive rights", "sexual rights", "reproductive health", "fertility regulation", "sexual health", "individuals", "sexual education and services for minors", "abortion in all its forms", "distribution of contraceptives" and "safe motherhood"</p></blockquote></span>
